<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Chicken</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the culinary use of chickens, see <a href="/wiki/Chicken_as_food" title="Chicken as food">Chicken as food</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Chicken_(disambiguation)" title="Chicken (disambiguation)">Chicken (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Chooks_(disambiguation)" title="Chooks (disambiguation)">Chooks (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center; font-size: 88%">Chicken distribution
</td></tr>

<p>The <b>chicken</b> (<i><b>Gallus gallus domesticus</b></i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domesticated</a> <a href="/wiki/Junglefowl" title="Junglefowl">junglefowl</a> species, with attributes of wild species such as the <a href="/wiki/Grey_junglefowl" title="Grey junglefowl">grey</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon_junglefowl" title="Ceylon junglefowl">Ceylon junglefowl</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawal-et-al-2020-and-revs_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lawal-et-al-2020-and-revs-1">[1]</a></sup> that are originally from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Asia" title="Southeastern Asia">Southeastern Asia</a>. <b>Rooster</b> or <b>cock</b> is a term for an adult male bird, and a younger male may be called a <b>cockerel</b>. A male that has been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castrated" title="Castrated">castrated</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Capon" title="Capon">capon</a>. An adult female bird is called a <b>hen</b> and a sexually immature female is called a <b>pullet</b>.
</p><p>Originally raised for <a href="/wiki/Cockfight" title="Cockfight">cockfighting</a> or for special ceremonies, chickens were not kept for food until the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a> (4th–2nd centuries BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr.org_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid26195775_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid26195775-3">[3]</a></sup> Humans now keep chickens primarily as a source of food (consuming both their <a href="/wiki/Chicken_as_food" title="Chicken as food">meat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egg_as_food" title="Egg as food">eggs</a>) and as <a href="/wiki/Pet" title="Pet">pets</a>.
</p><p>Chickens are one of the most common and widespread <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_animals" title="Domestic animals">domestic animals</a>, with a total population of 23.7 billion as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chicken&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> up from more than 19 billion in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011-19-billion-chickens_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011-19-billion-chickens-5">[5]</a></sup> There are more chickens in the world than any other <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">bird</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011-19-billion-chickens_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011-19-billion-chickens-5">[5]</a></sup> There are numerous <a href="/wiki/Cultural_references_to_chickens" title="Cultural references to chickens">cultural references to chickens</a> – in <a href="/wiki/Myth" title="Myth">myth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>.
</p><p>Genetic studies have pointed to multiple maternal origins in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, Southeast Asia, and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xiang_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Xiang-6">[6]</a></sup> but the <a href="/wiki/Clade" title="Clade">clade</a> found in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> originated from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>. From <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_India" title="Ancient India">ancient India</a>, the chicken spread to <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydia</a> in western <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> by the 5th century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Fowl have been known in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> since the mid-15th century BC, with the "bird that gives birth every day" having come from the land between <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shinar" title="Shinar">Shinar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonia</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Annals_of_Thutmose_III" title="Annals of Thutmose III">annals of Thutmose III</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RoehrigDreyfus2005_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-RoehrigDreyfus2005-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chicken_anatomy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2416" data-file-width="3609" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Chicken_anatomy.jpg/220px-Chicken_anatomy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Chicken_anatomy.jpg/330px-Chicken_anatomy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Chicken_anatomy.jpg/440px-Chicken_anatomy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chicken_anatomy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Educational_toy" title="Educational toy">Didactic model</a> of a chicken.</div></div></div>
<p>An adult male is a called a <i>cock</i> or (in the United States) a <i>rooster</i> and an adult female is called a <i>hen</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other terms are:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Biddy</i>: a newly hatched chicken<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Capon</i>: a castrated or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutered" title="Neutered">neutered</a> male chicken<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[a]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chick_(young_bird)" title="Chick (young bird)">Chick</a></i>: a young chicken<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Chook</i> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/tʃ/: 'ch' in 'China'">tʃ</span><span title="/ʊ/: 'u' in 'push'">ʊ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span>: a chicken (Australia/New Zealand, informal)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Cockerel</i>: a young male chicken less than a year old<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Dunghill fowl</i>: a chicken with mixed parentage from different domestic varieties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Pullet</i>: a young female chicken less than a year old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> In the poultry industry, a pullet is a sexually immature chicken less than 22 weeks of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Yardbird</i>: a chicken (southern United States, dialectal)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berhardt_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-berhardt-22">[21]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><i>Chicken</i> was originally a term only for an immature, or at least young, bird.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2021)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> In older sources, chicken as a species were typically referred to as <i>common fowl</i> or <i>domestic fowl</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2022)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2022)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p><i>Chicken</i> may also mean a <i>chick</i> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033199720">.mw-parser-output div.crossreference{padding-left:0}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference" role="note">(see for example <a href="/wiki/Hen_and_Chicken_Islands" title="Hen and Chicken Islands">Hen and Chicken Islands</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b> with: the origin of the term 'chicken' in general. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chicken&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>According to Merriam-Webster, the term <i>rooster</i> (i.e. a roosting bird) originated in the mid- or late 18th century as a euphemism to avoid the sexual connotation of the original English <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cock" title="wikt:cock">cock</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rawson_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rawson-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Online_Etymology_Dictionary_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Online_Etymology_Dictionary-27">[26]</a></sup> and is widely used throughout North America. <i>Roosting</i> is the action of perching aloft to sleep at night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_biology_and_habitat">General biology and habitat</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:302px;max-width:302px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rooster_portrait2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1334" decoding="async" height="450" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rooster_portrait2.jpg/300px-Rooster_portrait2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rooster_portrait2.jpg/450px-Rooster_portrait2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Rooster_portrait2.jpg/600px-Rooster_portrait2.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">In most breeds the adult <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rooster" title="Rooster">rooster</a> can be distinguished from the hen by his larger <a href="/wiki/Comb_(anatomy)" title="Comb (anatomy)">comb</a>.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:302px;max-width:302px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hen_Comb.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hen_Comb.jpg/300px-Hen_Comb.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hen_Comb.jpg/450px-Hen_Comb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hen_Comb.jpg/600px-Hen_Comb.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Comb_(anatomy)" title="Comb (anatomy)">Comb</a> of a hen.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Chickens are <a href="/wiki/Omnivore" title="Omnivore">omnivores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> In the wild, they often scratch at the soil to search for seeds, insects, and even animals as large as <a href="/wiki/Lizard" title="Lizard">lizards</a>, small snakes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> or sometimes young <a href="/wiki/Mouse" title="Mouse">mice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>The average chicken may live for 5–10 years, depending on the <a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">breed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> The world's oldest known chicken lived 16 years according to <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2387" data-file-width="3398" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg/200px-Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg/300px-Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg/400px-Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Didactic_model_of_a_chicken--FMVZ_USP-29.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Anatomy of a chicken.</div></div></div><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="301" data-file-width="514" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg/200px-Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg/300px-Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg/400px-Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cr%C3%A1neoAve.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diagram of a chicken skull.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3768" data-file-width="4632" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg/220px-Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg/330px-Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg/440px-Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eier_verschiedener_H%C3%BChnerrassen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eggs from different breeds</div></div></div>
<p>Roosters can usually be differentiated from hens by their striking plumage of long flowing tails and shiny, pointed feathers on their necks ('hackles') and backs ('saddle'), which are typically of brighter, bolder colours than those of females of the same breed. However, in some breeds, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sebright_chicken" title="Sebright chicken">Sebright chicken</a>, the rooster has only slightly pointed neck feathers, the same colour as the hen's. The identification can be made by looking at the <a href="/wiki/Comb_(anatomy)" title="Comb (anatomy)">comb</a>, or eventually from the development of spurs on the male's legs (in a few breeds and in certain hybrids, the male and female chicks may be differentiated by colour). Adult chickens have a fleshy crest on their heads called a comb, or cockscomb, and hanging flaps of skin either side under their beaks called <a href="/wiki/Wattle_(anatomy)" title="Wattle (anatomy)">wattles</a>. Collectively, these and other fleshy protuberances on the head and throat are called <a href="/wiki/Caruncle_(bird_anatomy)" title="Caruncle (bird anatomy)">caruncles</a>. Both the adult male and female have wattles and combs, but in most breeds these are more prominent in males.
A 'muff' or 'beard' is a <a href="/wiki/Mutation" title="Mutation">mutation</a> found in several chicken breeds which causes extra <a href="/wiki/Feather" title="Feather">feathering</a> under the chicken's face, giving the appearance of a <a href="/wiki/Beard" title="Beard">beard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plosg_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-plosg-34">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Domestic chickens are not capable of long-distance flight, although lighter chickens are generally capable of flying for short distances, such as over fences or into trees (where they would naturally roost). Chickens may occasionally fly briefly to explore their surroundings, but generally do so only to flee perceived danger.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Behavior">Behavior</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_behaviour">Social behaviour</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Empathy_in_chickens" title="Empathy in chickens">Empathy in chickens</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hen_with_chicks,_Raisen_district,_MP,_India.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2117" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg/302px-Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg/453px-Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg/604px-Hen_with_chicks%2C_Raisen_district%2C_MP%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="302"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hen_with_chicks,_Raisen_district,_MP,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hen with chicks, India</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:303px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_(36583204550).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="677" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg/301px-Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg/452px-Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg/602px-Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_%2836583204550%29.jpg 2x" width="301"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cascais_Costa_do_Esteril_52_(36583204550).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hen with chicks, Portugal</div></div></div>
<p>Chickens are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gregarious" title="Gregarious">gregarious</a> birds and live together in <a href="/wiki/Herd" title="Herd">flocks</a>. They have a communal approach to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avian_incubation" title="Avian incubation">incubation</a> of eggs and raising of young. Individual chickens in a flock will dominate others, establishing a '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pecking_order" title="Pecking order">pecking order</a>', with dominant individuals having priority for food access and nesting locations. Removing hens or roosters from a flock causes a temporary disruption to this social order until a new pecking order is established. Adding hens, especially younger birds, to an existing flock can lead to fighting and injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocalizations">Vocalizations</span></h4>
<p>When a rooster finds food, he may call other chickens to eat first. He does this by clucking in a high pitch as well as picking up and dropping the food. This behaviour may also be observed in mother hens to call their chicks and encourage them to eat.
</p><p>A rooster's crowing is a loud and sometimes shrill call and sends a territorial signal to other roosters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> However, roosters may also crow in response to sudden disturbances within their surroundings.
</p><p>Hens cluck loudly after laying an egg, and also to call their chicks. Chickens also give different warning calls when they sense a predator approaching from the air or on the ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Crowing">Crowing</span></h5>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Crowing"></span><span class="anchor" id="Cockadoodledoo"></span><span class="anchor" id="Cocka-doodle-doo"></span>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Cockadoodledoo" and "Cocka-doodle-doo" redirect here. For the nursery rhyme, see <a href="/wiki/Cock_a_doodle_doo" title="Cock a doodle doo">Cock a doodle doo</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:297px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canterino_Gallo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Canterino_Gallo.jpg/295px-Canterino_Gallo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Canterino_Gallo.jpg/443px-Canterino_Gallo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Canterino_Gallo.jpg/590px-Canterino_Gallo.jpg 2x" width="295"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canterino_Gallo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bergische_Kr%C3%A4her" title="Bergische Kräher">Bergische Kräher</a> crowing</div></div></div>

<p>Roosters almost always start crowing before four months of age. Although it is possible for a hen to crow as well, crowing (together with hackles development) is one of the clearest signs of being a rooster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Rooster_crowing_contests">Rooster crowing contests</span></h6>
<p>Rooster crowing contests, also known as crowing contests, are a traditional sport in several countries, such as Germany, the Netherlands, Belgium,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> the United States, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and Japan. The oldest contests are held with <a href="/wiki/Long-crowing_chicken" title="Long-crowing chicken">longcrowers</a>. Depending on the breed, either the duration of the crowing or the times the rooster crows within a certain time is measured.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Courtship">Courtship</span></h4>
<p>To initiate courting, some roosters may dance in a circle around or near a hen (a 'circle dance'), often lowering the wing which is closest to the hen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grandin69_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-grandin69-40">[39]</a></sup> The dance triggers a response in the hen<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grandin69_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-grandin69-40">[39]</a></sup> and when she responds to his 'call', the rooster may mount the hen and proceed with the mating.
</p><p>More specifically, mating typically involves the following sequence:
</p>
<ol><li>Male approaching the hen</li>
<li>Male pre-copulatory waltzing</li>
<li>Male waltzing</li>
<li>Female crouching (receptive posture) or stepping aside or running away (if unwilling to copulate)</li>
<li>Male mounting</li>
<li>Male treading with both feet on hen's back</li>
<li>Male tail bending (following successful copulation)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nesting_and_laying_behaviour">Nesting and laying behaviour</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:283px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chicken_eggs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chicken_eggs.jpg/281px-Chicken_eggs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chicken_eggs.jpg/422px-Chicken_eggs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Chicken_eggs.jpg/562px-Chicken_eggs.jpg 2x" width="281"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chicken_eggs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chicken <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_(biology)" title="Egg (biology)">eggs</a> vary in colour depending on the breed, and sometimes, the hen, typically ranging from bright white to shades of brown and even blue, green, light pinkish and recently reported purple (found in South Asia) (<a href="/wiki/Araucana" title="Araucana">Araucana</a> varieties).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:301px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg/299px-K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg/449px-K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg/598px-K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg 2x" width="299"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:K%C3%BCken_vor_dem_ersten_Ausflug.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chicks before their first outing</div></div></div>
<p>Hens will often try to lay in nests that already contain eggs and have been known to move eggs from neighbouring nests into their own. The result of this behaviour is that a flock will use only a few preferred locations, rather than having a different nest for every bird. Hens will often express a preference to lay in the same location. It is not unknown for two (or more) hens to try to share the same nest at the same time. If the nest is small, or one of the hens is particularly determined, this may result in chickens trying to lay on top of each other. There is evidence that individual hens prefer to be either solitary or gregarious nesters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:300px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1823" data-file-width="1292" decoding="async" height="421" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg/298px-%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg/448px-%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg/597px-%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg 2x" width="298"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B0%95%E0%B1%8B%E0%B0%A1%E0%B0%BF_%E0%B0%AA%E0%B0%BF%E0%B0%B2%E0%B1%8D%E0%B0%B2IMG20191207080730-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A chick sitting in a person's hand</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Broodiness">Broodiness</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chicken&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Under natural conditions, most birds lay only until a <a href="/wiki/Clutch_(eggs)" title="Clutch (eggs)">clutch</a> is complete, and they will then incubate all the eggs. Hens are then said to "go <a href="/wiki/Broodiness" title="Broodiness">broody</a>". The broody hen will stop laying and instead will focus on the incubation of the eggs (a full clutch is usually about 12 eggs). She will sit or 'set' on the nest, fluffing up or pecking in defense if disturbed or removed. The hen will rarely leave the nest to eat, drink, or dust-bathe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puff-up-Feathers_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puff-up-Feathers-43">[42]</a></sup> While brooding, the hen maintains the nest at a constant temperature and humidity, as well as turning the eggs regularly during the first part of the incubation. To stimulate broodiness, owners may place several artificial eggs in the nest. To discourage it, they may place the hen in an elevated cage with an open wire floor.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="688" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png/200px-1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png/300px-1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png/400px-1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1911_EB_Chicken_skull.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skull of a three-week-old chicken. Here the opisthotic bone appears in the occipital region, as in the adult Chelonian. bo = Basi-occipital, bt = Basi-temporal, eo = Opisthotic, f = Frontal, fm = Foramen magnum, fo = Fontanella, oc = Occipital condyle, op = Opisthotic, p = Parietal, pf = Post-frontal, sc = Sinus canal in supra-occipital, so = Supra-occpital, sq = Squamosal, 8 = Exit of vagus nerve.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">Breeds</a> artificially developed for <a href="/wiki/Egg_as_food" title="Egg as food">egg production</a> rarely go broody, and those that do often stop part-way through the incubation. However, other breeds, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cochin_(chicken)" title="Cochin (chicken)">Cochin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cornish_(chicken)" title="Cornish (chicken)">Cornish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silkie_(chicken)" title="Silkie (chicken)">Silkie</a>, do regularly go broody, and make excellent mothers, not only for chicken eggs but also for those of other species — even those with much smaller or larger eggs and different incubation periods, such as <a href="/wiki/Quail" title="Quail">quail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pheasant" title="Pheasant">pheasants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_duck" title="Domestic duck">ducks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkeys</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">geese</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hatching_and_early_life">Hatching and early life</span></h4>
<p>Fertile chicken eggs hatch at the end of the incubation period, about 21 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grandin69_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-grandin69-40">[39]</a></sup> Development of the chick starts only when incubation begins, so all chicks hatch within a day or two of each other, despite perhaps being laid over a period of two weeks or so. Before hatching, the hen can hear the chicks peeping inside the eggs, and will gently cluck to stimulate them to break out of their shells. The chick begins by 'pipping'; pecking a breathing hole with its <a href="/wiki/Egg_tooth" title="Egg tooth">egg tooth</a> towards the blunt end of the egg, usually on the upper side. The chick then rests for some hours, absorbing the remaining egg yolk and withdrawing the blood supply from the membrane beneath the shell (used earlier for breathing through the shell). The chick then enlarges the hole, gradually turning round as it goes, and eventually severing the blunt end of the shell completely to make a lid. The chick crawls out of the remaining shell, and the wet <a href="/wiki/Down_feather" title="Down feather">down</a> dries out in the warmth of the nest.
</p><p>Hens usually remain on the nest for about two days after the first chick hatches, and during this time the newly hatched chicks feed by absorbing the internal <a href="/wiki/Yolk_sac" title="Yolk sac">yolk sac</a>. Some breeds sometimes start eating cracked eggs, which can become habitual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Hens fiercely guard their chicks, and brood them when necessary to keep them warm, at first often returning to the nest at night. She leads them to food and water and will call them toward edible items, but seldom feeds them directly. She continues to care for them until they are several weeks old.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defensive_behaviour">Defensive behaviour</span></h4>
<p>Chickens may occasionally gang up on a weak or inexperienced predator. At least one credible report exists of a young fox killed by hens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> A group of hens have been recorded in attacking a <a href="/wiki/Hawk" title="Hawk">hawk</a> that had entered their coop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>If a chicken is threatened by predators, stress, or is sick, there is a chance that they will puff up their feathers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puff-up-Feathers_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Puff-up-Feathers-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reproduction">Reproduction</span></h3>
<p>Sperm transfer occurs by <a href="/wiki/Cloaca" title="Cloaca">cloacal</a> contact between the male and female, in a maneuver known as the 'cloacal kiss'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Briskie1997_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Briskie1997-49">[48]</a></sup> As with birds in general, reproduction is controlled by a <a href="/wiki/Neuroendocrine_cell" title="Neuroendocrine cell">neuroendocrine</a> system, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gonadotropin-Releasing_Hormone-I_neuron" title="Gonadotropin-Releasing Hormone-I neuron">Gonadotropin-Releasing Hormone-I neurons</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamus" title="Hypothalamus">hypothalamus</a>. Locally to the <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_system" title="Reproductive system">reproductive system</a> itself, reproductive hormones such as <a href="/wiki/Estrogen" title="Estrogen">estrogen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Progesterone" title="Progesterone">progesterone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonadotropin" title="Gonadotropin">gonadotropins</a> (<a href="/wiki/Luteinizing_hormone" title="Luteinizing hormone">luteinizing hormone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Follicle-stimulating_hormone" title="Follicle-stimulating hormone">follicle-stimulating hormone</a>) initiate and maintain sexual maturation changes. Over time there is reproductive decline, thought to be due to GnRH-I-N decline. Because there is significant inter-individual variability in egg-producing duration, it is believed to be possible to breed for further extended useful lifetime in egg-layers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bain-et-al-2016_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bain-et-al-2016-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Embryology">Embryology</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:255px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="290" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Embryo.ogv" height="190" id="mwe_player_2" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Embryo.ogv/253px--Embryo.ogv.jpg" preload="none" width="253"><source data-bandwidth="449680" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="300" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file, 400 × 300 (450 kbps)" data-width="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Embryo.ogv" type='video/ogg; codecs="theora"'/><source data-bandwidth="53640" data-framerate="29.97" data-height="120" data-shorttitle="VP9 120P" data-title="Lowest bandwidth VP9 (120P)" data-transcodekey="120p.vp9.webm" data-width="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/d/d2/Embryo.ogv/Embryo.ogv.120p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm;
